                                 Books by the Author
1. 3D Unconditional Security—graphical overview of principle perspectives regarding unconditional security.
2. 4D Forgiveness—examines four levels of biblical forgiveness and explains how it is possible for God to
    forgive and forget our sin in one stratum while not forgiving or forgetting our sin in another stratum.
3. Breaking the Rocking Horse—introductory book regarding the distinction between having eternal life as a
    gift versus obtaining it as a reward in relation to the outer darkness and the parable of the soils.
4. Carnal Corinth—an affirmation of the categorical existence of carnal Corinthian Christians.
5. Destined for Salvation—evaluates five major models for interpreting 1Thess 5:9-10 and takes the passage
    as promising an unconditional rapture (and thus unconditional security) to all believers in Christ, even to
    those who are morally asleep. However, an incentive for being morally awake is provided by making
    salvation (in the form of millennial and eternal rulership) contingent upon being morally alert.
6. Fallen from Grace but Not from Perfection—an advanced defense of unconditional security which affirms
    that believers can fall from grace but not fall from perfection.
7. Is God a Communist?—by comparing Paul’s teaching of the workmen with Jesus’ parable of the laborers,
    this book refutes communistic views of Heaven which think that Jesus is building heavenly mansions in
    New Jerusalem for all believers regardless of the way they live.
8. John in Living Color—a color-coded translation and reference manual of the Gospel of John that focuses
    on the grammatical and aspectual indications of unconditional security.
9. Like a Tree Planted by the Water—expounds upon the OT background for the outer darkness by examining
    the precursor texts in Psalms, especially Ps 1-2.
10. Logic Tables and Diagrams—illustrations of logic with scriptural implications pertaining primarily to the
    soteriological and misthological arenas.
11. Mere Christianity and Moral Christianity—a more comprehensive discussion regarding perseverance (and
    other performance-related themes) as being needed for rewards in Heaven rather than for entrance into
    Heaven. This book provides both introductory material and advanced treatments.
12. Monogamous Sex in Heaven!—at the same time in which the present author was reading books by Marrow
    and Kreeft posing that sexual intimacy continues in Heaven, he discovered that his wife had stage-3 breast
    cancer. As a therapy to help him deal with this news, he poured himself into research to see if Marrow and
    Kreeft might be correct, thereby enabling him to believe that no matter what happened, the best was yet to
    come. This is the conclusion and comfort of this book.
13. New Birth by the Sovereign Wind—refutes the Calvinistic interpretation of Jn 3:16 that limits God’s love
    to the elect. An excursus deals with the Calvinistic claim from Jn 3:3 that one must be born again before
    one can see (i.e., believe) the gospel. An additional excursus entertains a possible duality to what it means
    to see the kingdom.
14. Predestination and the Open View—a discussion of predestination that focuses on free will and the book
    of life from an open view.
15. Rewards are Eternal—is a defense of the eternal nature of biblical rewards against the proposition that
    Rev 22:5 indicates that all believers will rule in the eternal state and against the premise that Rev 21:4
    proves that misthological death will no longer exist in the eternal state.
16. Sealed and Secure—a thorough defense of a popular argument for unconditional security that also defends
    the premise of unconditional promises.
17. The Race of Grace—introductory book in which performance-related themes (such as perseverance) are
    considered essential for rewards in Heaven. Entrance into Heaven, in contrast, is regarded as free. A strong
    defense of unconditional security derived from believers being given to Jesus is a strength of this book.
18. The Outer Darkness—a magnum opus that ties together the author’s arguments for unconditional security
    and conditional rewards.
19. Trichotomy—an advanced holistic dichotomous discussion of trichotomy with an integration of nikology.
20. Woolly Wolves and Woolless Sheep—a rejection of the notion that profession of salvation is proven genuine
    by the way a person lives. This book focuses on the parable of the sheep and the goats and shows the
    inadequacy of conditional security in interpreting this parable.
                      For books by the author, see http://misthology.org/?page_id=35.
                        For additional material, see www.UnconditionalSecurity.org.

Asia, is also thanked for her assistance. Scott Crawford’s model of the intermediate state was most helpful in
formulating a competing model to my own and, ultimately, to proposing a more satisfying synthesis. Our friend,
James Hollandsworth, has being helpful in proofreading this mediation, and his own model has been used, in part,
in a mediation pertaining to multiple vantage points. Our friend, Martha Lever, must also be thanked for her

                                  Chapter 1. New Jerusalem
                                                   Introduction
       As noted in Part 1 of this series, some matters, but not all, as Dillow remarked, are best left to speculation.
Part 2 will move into highly speculative fields to present possible scenarios for less speculative hypotheses. After
all, as Dillow also correctly stated, it is incumbent upon the interpreter to present plausible scenarios for their
models. Part 1 sought to provide plausible scenarios for the three best competing macromisthological models of the
outer darkness. All three of these models implement a literal view of New Jerusalem and a corresponding spatial
view of the outer darkness. The superiority of the literal-spatial hermeneutic is not a matter of mere speculation;
rather, it is derived from superior inductive and deductive probability, logical consistency, and mathematical
computation. Part 2 will continue with a defense of literality regarding rewards in this faceoff between my magnum
opus, The Outer Darkness, and Dillow’s, Final Destiny.1 Since the initial release of our books at the same time,
Dillow has refined his arguments in subsequent editions of Destiny. I have refined my arguments by releasing
additional books, such as the books in this present series. The present book will give a brief rehash of these
arguments and then move into new territory.
                                            The Death of Procreation
      The difference in the degree to which Dillow and I interpret such matters literally also surfaces when the
matter of human procreation in the eternal state is considered.

            Obviously, this future kingdom embraces the entire created order. One day mankind will conquer
       the galaxies! While it is true that one purpose of the heavens was to “declare the glory of God,” it
       seems that they were also created to be placed in subjection to man. Perhaps the future kingdom with
       its reign of universal righteousness and perfect government will result in a technological explosion as
       well as a spiritual one. Then and only then, in submission to the King, will man be able to achieve his
       fondest dreams, to rule and have dominion. (Destiny, 956.)

The natural presumption would be that mankind will continue to expand numerically through procreation in order
to rule the enlarged territory. After all, there are far more galaxies than there are humans. Yet Dillow oddly
presumes differently. He rejects the proposal that believers who live to the end of the millennial kingdom will be
able to enter the eternal state in sinless flesh and blood bodies in order to procreate and populate the ever-increasing
kingdom. As a result, he even denies that the healing affirmed in Rev 22:2 applies to the eternal state, even though
that is the time period in which the context places it. He attempts to deliteralize this verse by claiming, “In the new
heavens and the new earth the leaves of the tree of life provide ‘healing for the nations.’ This ‘healing’ refers
retrospectively to the healing that has already occurred through the cross of Christ” (Destiny, 119, n. 398). Nonliteral
healing from the nonliteral leaves of a nonliteral tree that produces nonliteral fruit in a retrospective season is
Dillow’s perspective!2 An amillennialist would be proud. In contrast, being true to my dispensational framework,
my propensity is to take the Bible literally unless the literal sense does not make sense. And I have no trouble
believing that the tree of life is a literal tree that produces literal fruit that one can really eat and that the tree bears
literal leaves that provide physical healing. Dillow wants to spiritualize away such physical possibilities. In this
same footnote, he further seeks to do away with the possibility of physical, natural bodies in the eternal state:



1
  Joseph C. Dillow, Final Destiny: The Future Reign of the Servant Kings, 20th edition (Monument, CO: Paniym
Group, 2014).
2
  One reason that Dillow would have the propensity to treat the tree of life as a mere symbol rather than a literal
reality is because once you admit that the tree of life is literal, you must affirm that it has spatial attributes. In other
words, you must have some place—a literal, spatial place—to put the tree. But then you are led to infer that since
subcomers are excluded from the tree of life, they are excluded from the place where the tree of life is located. This
inference immediately leads to assigning spatial value to the outer darkness, as the place of exclusion from the tree
of life. In short, for misthologists, a literal tree presupposes a spatial outer darkness. If you cannot have a spatial
outer darkness, then you cannot have a literal tree. Conversely, if the tree is literal, then the place of misthological
exclusion from that tree is spatial.
Page 2                                                                                  Misthological Models: Part 2
      There is no room here for two kinds of bodies in the eternal state, enhanced mortal bodies which do
      not need healing but can have broken bones and the glorified resurrection bodies mentioned elsewhere.
      These bodies are “imperishable.” They are like Jesus’ body in His resurrection (Philippians 3:21),
      physical but glorified and indestructible. There can be no physical wounds because this would involve
      deterioration and death of flesh or bone cells which must then be replaced. Death has been forever
      removed at the beginning of the eternal state [Rev 21:4].3

       Darkness (ch. 28), in contrast, provides numerous reasons from a number of writers in defense of the
proposition that human procreation will continue in the eternal state. Since that release, as I noted in my subsequent
release of Monogamous Sex in Heaven (MSIH), Sterling has written an excellent three-part series of articles
discussing the possibility of two modes of humanity in the eternal state.4 As I stated in the introduction of MSIH, I
emailed Sterling a copy of my book, Rewards are Eternal (RAE), with this explanation:

             I enjoyed your articles in JOTGES. As you noted, Dillow rejects the two-mode view of
      humanity in the eternal state. As you suggested, perhaps Platonic views lay behind his objection.
      Nevertheless, the heart of his argument, as he has stated it, is that procreation cannot occur in the
      eternal state because there is no form of death in the eternal state. Although Dillow affirms that rewards
      are eternal, his no-death position necessarily leads to a rejection of rewards altogether in the eternal
      state. He is not aware of this inconsistency. But others have used this same argument to deny that
      rewards are eternal. Therefore, I had to refute Dillow’s argument in my book, Rewards are Eternal.5

       Admittedly, the new Dillowian variation of his objection did not make the list of objections refuted by
Darkness.6 Yet Darkness did rebut the Chitwoodian form of this objection which states: “There can be no such
thing as Christians being hurt of the second death beyond the Millennium, for Rev. 21:4 plainly declares that there
will be no more death during this time.”7 The arguments of both Dillow and Chitwood stand or fall together.
                                           The Death of Eternal Rewards
      In Mysteries, Chitwood has extrapolated his argument to deduce, correctly, that accepting his argument
against death leads to the death of eternal rewards. Below is his argument quoted at length:

             Christ and His co-heirs, beyond the Millennium, will no longer rule over the nations, as this rule
      is pictured in Rev. 2:26, 27. Rather, the Gentiles comprising the nations will be brought into positions
      of rulership themselves with Christ and His co-heirs, as this rule extends beyond the earth, out into the
      universe (Rev 22:2, 5). And the Son, beyond the Millennium, will no longer sit on His Own throne, as
      seen in Rev. 3:21. Rather, He will sit on “the throne of God and of the Lamb,” from whence universal
      rule will emanate (Rev. 22:1, 3, 5).

3
  Dillow, Destiny, 119-120, n. 398. Dillow’s statement is a nonsensical strawman caricature. Who is posing that
those who enter the eternal state in enhanced physical bodies can have a broken bone but not need healing?
Obviously, if you have a broken bone, you need healing!

              It is the overcomer’s promise to the Church in Smyrna which has to do with the lake of fire,
      something which can only be millennial within its scope of fulfillment. That is, the conditions alluded
      to for the nonovercomer in this promise will exist for the duration of the Messianic Era, not throughout
      the eternal ages beyond.
              Scripture deals with millennial rewards and/or loss, never with eternal rewards and/or loss. This
      should be easy enough for anyone to understand, for if rewards are eternal, so is loss of rewards. And
      loss of rewards involves an association with death (Rom. 8:13), something which the Scripture clearly
      reveals will be done away with at the beginning of the eternal ages beyond the Millennium
      (1 Cor. 15:26; Rev. 21:4).
              The overcomer’s promise to those Christians comprising the Church in Smyrna reads,

             “He that hath an ear, let him hear what the Spirit saith unto the churches; He that
             overcometh shall not be hurt of the second death” (2:11; cf. Rev. 20:6).

              There is a clear implication in this promise that those who do not overcome will be hurt of the
      second death. And any attempt to take this promise and make it mean something other than what it
      clearly states serves only to destroy the promise, something which the Lord sounded a solemn warning
      against (Rev. 22:18, 19). The promise that those who do overcome will not “be hurt of the second
      death” would be meaningless unless this promise is taken at face value and allowed to mean exactly
      what it says, clearly implying that those who do not overcome will “be hurt of the second death.”
              “The second death” in the Book of Revelation is associated with the lake of fire (Rev. 21:8).
      And those who do not overcome (v. 7) are going to have their part in this lake of fire (v. 8). That is,
      they will be hurt of the second death by having a part in the lake of fire....
              To distinguish between millennial and eternal conditions in this respect, note that those outside
      the gates during the eternal ages will be the Gentile nations, as the New Jerusalem rests on the new
      earth (21:24-27); but those outside the gates during the preceding Messianic Era, with the New
      Jerusalem in the heavens above the earth, will be the nonovercomers (22:14, 15). And the place which
      they will occupy is described at least four other ways in Scripture — through the use of Gehenna, the
      outer darkness, the furnace of fire, and the lake of fire....
              Through comparing Scripture with Scripture, it is plain that these are simply different ways of
      expressing the same thing. And since a literal casting into outer darkness, Gehenna, or a furnace or
      lake of fire could not possibly be in view (for these different places could not possibly be looked upon
      as referring to the same place in a literal sense), it is evident that metaphors are being used throughout.
      But relative to the unsaved and the lake of fire, this is simply not expressed other ways in Scripture as
      it is with the saved, leaving no room for any thought other than understanding the matter as literal, not
      metaphorical. Aside from the preceding, it is clear that all Christians, faithful and unfaithful alike, will
      be in the kingdom. This is seen in type in Genesis chapters eighteen and nineteen. Both Abraham and
      Lot, in the final analysis, are seen on the mount (a “mountain” in Scripture signifies a kingdom). But
      note the stark difference in the place which each occupied. Abraham stood before the Lord, where he
      had always stood (18:22; 19:27). Lot though found himself in a place separated from the Lord, in a
      place where he also had always stood (19:1, 30). (Emphasis his.)8

       Ironically, Dillow, who affirms eternal rewards, unwittingly uses the same argument against eternal
procreation that Chitwood implements against eternal rewards. Yet their arguments mutually nullify each another.
Their joint premise is that no form of death will occur in the eternal state because no death will occur in the eternal
state. Let us go back to the biblical beginning and see if such an argument made sense even then. At the conclusion
of this study, a more detailed interaction with Chitwood’s argument against eternal rewards will be provided. For
now it suffices to kill it, along with Dillow’s contention, with a rabbit observation.

reasonably, the acknowledgement that we can eat fish leads to the affirmation of a food chain.11 The riddle of

starlight is supposed to be one of the major problems for Young Earth Creationism (YEC). For myself, though, I

simpler question: “What about the rabbits?” If there is no food chain and procreation is to continue, then would not
the planet quickly become overpopulated by animals? The jackrabbit drives associated with the Dust Bowl during
the Great Depression were a matter of survival for farmers in western Kansas.12 Since the farmers had killed the
coyotes, the natural food chain was no longer in place to control the rabbit population. Are we left to believe that
reproduction stops in the millennial and eternal kingdom when the population of any species reaches optimum
capacity, so that the God who loves the little children will have no room for children in the eternal state? Surely
not! So how is one to suppose that procreation will continue but overpopulation will not be a problem? If Copan’s
interpretation is correct, then the food chain could still be in effect in the millennial and eternal state. In fact,
according to the OT, the Passover is celebrated by the Jews throughout their generations as a permanent, everlasting
ordinance forever (Ex 12:14,17,42; NAS; NKJ; ESV). The celebration of this feast, in the manner in which it is
prescribed, necessarily involves killing and eating the Passover lamb. If these texts are taken at face value, they
clinch the argument that we will eat slain meat, not only in the millennial kingdom but also in the eternal state.
Therefore, reproduction need not cease. Nor, for that matter, would one need to pose the necessity of a food
synthesizer to produce meat in order to have lamb chops or steak in that case. On the other hand, one might allow
both possibilities: food chain and food synthesizer. The latter would be a very convenient device aboard starships,
for example. Space travel and starships are a given. For mankind to rule the galaxies intergalactical space travel
must happen. The rabbit question must be addressed not only by those who believe in eternal procreation but also
by those who acknowledge millennial procreation and the YEC model. Given that much time, would the Garden of
Eden, and the planet for that matter, be overrun by rabbits?
       We know that death entered the world through sin (Rom 5:12). From a YEC perspective, I would understand
this to mean that there was no death, in this biblical sense, before Adam and Eve sinned. But does this mean that
there was no death in any sense before Adam and Eve sinned? In Dillowian logic, Adam and Eve could not suffer
physical wounds because this would involve deterioration and death of flesh or bone cells which must then be
replaced! And we know this to be so, according to Dillow, because death never existed in the world until Adam
and Eve sinned. So, given this Dillowian premise, are we to assume that Adam and Eve could not so much as suffer
a scratch or a scrape before they sinned? But if that is the case, then how is it that their bodies were impervious to
injury? Did they have imperishable, indestructible bodies like Jesus’ resurrection body!?! Obviously, they did not!

But one cannot stop there. Given this Dillowian premise, no death of any type anywhere can be allowed that would
involve the replacement of flesh and bone cells. Thus, given that perspective, not even animals could experience
scratches or scrapes! Did they have resurrection bodies too!?!
       Dill defends RET (Ruined-Earth Theory) against YEC (Young Earth Creationism) by explaining that death
must have been in place before the fall:

      Over the years, I have seen Young-Earth creationists repeatedly try to destroy the Gap Theory by using
      a particular “biblical bombshell” that “proves” they are right. Let me defuse this “bomb.” Young-Earth
      creationists insist that the Restoration Theory is wrong because it means death reigned before Adam.
      Gap Theory creationists look at the geological strata and say that all those fossils (dead things) were
      formed before Adam was created. Young-Earth creationists become indignant when they hear this.
      They believe there was no death before Adam sinned. “By one man sin entered into the world, and
      death by sin,” they’ll quote. According to them, Romans 5:12 and 1 Corinthians 15:21 prove there was
      no death before Adam sinned. If you question them, however, they usually admit that some kind of
      death must have existed before Adam's fall. Plants died when eaten. Cows didn’t carry microscopes to
      pick off the microscopic mites living on the blades of grass before they ate. These mites would have
      been killed by the cow’s digestion system. Insects, nematodes, and other soil-living creatures got
      squished as great herds of buffalo crossed the plains. Plankton-feeding whales would have digested
      microscopic animals along with microscopic plants. Once something is digested, it’s pretty good and
      dead. The outer-most layer of epithelial tissue (skin) consists of cells that are dead. If those skin cells
      were alive, we would be in excruciating pain every time something touched us, and worse than that,
      we would dehydrate within hours. The layer of dead epithelial cells acts as a fluid barrier to prevent
      desiccation. If those cells weren’t dead, we soon would be! Furthermore, those dead cells are
      constantly being rubbed off and replaced by the growing cells beneath them. Epithelial cells aren’t the
      only cells continually dying in order for animals to live. Red blood cells have a constant turnover rate.
      White blood cells do the same. Osteoclasts are cells that continually kill bone cells so that new bone
      cells can be made by osteoblasts. If this didn’t happen, bones couldn’t grow. Baby animals couldn’t
      become adult animals if living cells didn’t die. If you study embryological development, you’ll
      discover that certain embryonic cells have to die in order for further development to take place.
      Without death, animals couldn’t have multiplied according to God’s command. There had to be death
      of some kind, even in animals.13

      As for myself, I am intrigued by both RET and YEC. For the purposes of this present inquiry, it is not
necessary to choose between the two. Indeed, one could even combine the two into a YRE (Young Ruined Earth).
Simply put the creation at 10,000 years ago and pose a 4,000 gap before Adam was created, with the Luciferian fall
and the destruction of Earth occurring during that time frame. In any event, both OEC (Old-Earth Creationists) and
YEC (Young Earth Creationists) generally concur that some form of death occurred before Adam’s fall and was
even operational in the Garden of Eden before the fall.14 This conclusion is logically necessary. But if some form

of death was occurring in flesh and blood creatures, at least at the molecular level, then the Dillowian-Chitwoodian

       But why stop with flesh and blood creatures in responding to Dillow or Chitwood? The Dillowian-
Chitwoodian premise rules out any and all forms of death does it not? Otherwise, if some forms of death are
permitted, then one could argue that the form of death which takes place in cell reproduction after an injury is
permissible. However, if all forms of death are excluded, as Dillow and Chitwood are advocating, then even the
death of plant life is excluded. In that case, Adam could not so much as pick a flower and give to Eve in the Garden
of Eden because that would have involved the death of the flower, which strictly would be prohibited by the
extension of the Dillowian-Chitwoodian argument. One cannot stop there, however; for according to Jesus “unless
a grain of wheat falls into the earth and dies, it remains by itself alone; but if it dies, it bears much fruit” (Jn 12:24).
Biblically speaking, then, even this form of plant reproduction involves a form of death. So are we to conclude that
such reproduction among plant life did not come into being until after the fall? Of course not! Biblical reproduction
nullifies the Dillowian-Chitwoodian prohibition. Applying the same set of arguments to the eternal state is simple.
Will wheat still grow in the eternal state? Yes. Will animals still exist in the eternal state? Yes. They are part of the
creation that groans for the transformation. Yet one need not suppose that they necessarily will be in imperishable,
indestructible, resurrected bodies! Much more reasonable is the proposition that the absence of the death does not
rule out all forms of death, only the forms of death intended by the original author. Dillow and Chitwood have
moved beyond the original intent of the text. The Dillowian-Chitwoodian proposition is falsified. Dillow’s objection
may be safely added to the list of failed protests against human procreation in the eternal state. I still have not
encountered any valid objection against the proposition that the human population will continue to expand in the
eternal state, nor have I encountered any valid objection against eternal rewards, and that assessment includes
Chitwood’s tree-of-life argument.
       Chitwood seeks to use the tree of life to refute the eternal nature of rewards by stating:

           Man was created in the beginning to rule and to reign. And though only a part of saved mankind will
    have been brought back into a position to occupy the throne at the beginning of the Millennium (with the
    tree of life made available to them at this time), at the end of the Millennium the whole of saved mankind
    will be brought back into this [ruling and reigning] position (with the tree of life made available to
    them at this time).15 (Italics his.)

Supposedly, after 1000 years, per Chitwood’s claim as stated here, it will no longer matter if you lived for the Lord
during your life on Earth because all of saved humanity is going to rule with the Lord and have access to the tree of
life during the eternal state. Thus, in such Chitwoodian misthology, after unfaithful believers have been in the outer
darkness for 1000 years, they will co-rule with Christ for the remainder of eternity.16 Rewards are only temporary,
lasting only for the fleeting millennium. Thereafter, unfaithful and faithful believers share and share alike in a
communistic Heaven. Chitwood’s justification for this assessment is based on his rendering of Rev 22:2:

               This whole overall thought concerning the tree of life in Scripture would have to hold true, for
       that seen relative to this tree in Revelation chapter two is drawn from that which was first seen relative
       to this tree in Genesis chapters two and three. The fruit of the tree of life was in the past (seen in the
       Book of Genesis) and will be in the future (seen in the Book of Revelation) a provision for the rulers
       in the kingdom. This is an evident fact which must be recognized.
               And, in that coming day following the Millennium, the tree of life will be for “the healing of
       the nations” (Rev. 22:2). The Greek word translated “healing” is therapeia, from which the English
       word “therapy” is derived. This is a medical term which has to do with restorative healing. In that day,
       God will restore all of saved mankind to the original place which man occupied at the time of his
       creation. And, consequently, the whole of saved mankind, with regality in view, will have access to the

insect level. Moreover, fish and birds would have been able to eat insects. The debate, then, seems to be over the
scope rather than possibility of a pre-fall food chain.

        Chitwood correctly perceives that the fruit of the tree of life was originally only given regally to kingdom
rulers in both Genesis and Revelation. The fruit of the tree of life is a reward; therefore, it is not available freely or
universally to all believers. Splendid! However, he then erroneously takes away a key detail from the biblical text
in his ongoing discussion to derive his errant opinion that the fruit of the tree of life is subsequently made available
freely to all believers within the eternal state. On the one hand, the Bible says that the leaves of the tree will be for
the healing of the nations. Chitwood, contrariwise, says that the tree will be for the healing of the nations. He has
distorted the biblical message by leaving out a crucial detail. By leaving out the leaves in Rev 22:2, he has made
the unwarranted extrapolation that the fruit of the tree must no longer be a reward limited to the faithful, as it was
in Rev 2:7, since the tree is now given allegedly to nations that did not earn a right to the tree in Rev 22:2. Never
mind that the tree of life is still a reward a few verses later in Rev 22:14,19! Chitwood has abused both the text
and the context.18 He assumes, without any justification, that being given the leaves of the tree entails the right to
eat the fruit of the tree. But the leaves are not the fruit; moreover, the leaves could be harvested and exported to the
nations without giving the nations direct access to the tree of life. With such unwarranted jumps in logic, he then
proceeds to presume that all believers will eat the fruit and thus rule the Earth.
        In addition to these types of errors, Chitwood fails to notice that the leaves may die after they have been
gathered from the tree to be applied to the nations. This type of death still occurs in the eternal state. The leaves of
the tree of life do not have eternal life in that they do not live forever. The tree of life does not die, but its leaves do.
For that matter, most plants probably will still be subject to death, even in the eternal state. Certainly, the plants we
eat will be subject to death. This observation, by the way, destroys Chitwood’s other argument against eternal
rewards, which is based on his faulty premise that no death of any type will exist in the eternal state, which leads
him to make the defective inference that misthological death cannot exist during the millennial state, which in turn
leads to his fallacious conclusion that rewards cannot continue in the eternal state. Terribly erroneous conclusions
can be reached when one takes away from the biblical text by leaving out the leaves.19
        In summary, Dillow wrongly thinks that the leaves of the tree do not provide healing during the eternal
state, while Chitwood rightly acknowledges that the eternal state is in preview. Inversely, Chitwood incorrectly
fails to perceive that some form of death necessarily is inferred by being hurt physically in the eternal state,
while Dillow astutely deduces that some form of death is involved inescapably in being hurt physically. Their
offsetting arguments readily lead to the proper conclusion: Human procreation, healing, and rewards will continue
during the eternal state.20

        In the eternal state, human death will be impossible, even apart from the literal leaves of this literal tree. The
leaves will just enhance the response of the enhanced natural bodies of the nations that are functioning at full, sinless
capacity. Being a fan of the Wolverine from X-Men, I interjected this sci-fi personality into Alcorn’s explanation
above to help us imagine what Alcorn is describing. Technically, however, clarification is prudent: Eating the leaves
of that tree will not impart beneficial genetic mutations, such as what is found in the fictional Wolverine. Our planet
is facing a very dangerous time in which science fiction is quickly becoming science fact. The genetic
experimentation of today is rapidly giving rise to transhumanism with the goal to posthumanism. The human race
is in danger of introducing genetic modifications on a mass scale that will result in our species becoming something
other than purely human—almost human will become increasingly nonhuman. Genetic Armageddon looms on the
horizon in which human beings will turn themselves into modern day Nephilim—genetic mutations that cannot be
redeemed because they are not truly human. Once these mutations start becoming introduced into society on the
broad scale, there will be no going back. If the Lord were to tarry, no human race (as we know it) would be left for
Him to come back to; therefore, the most reasonable projections cannot place His return in the far future.
Consequently, the calculations in the present series for the number of inhabitants for New Jerusalem cannot be off
by any significant factor. For example, the Lord will not be able to delay His return for another two thousand years
since a significant delay is becoming increasingly impossible. Along that same token, the leaves of the tree of life
certainly will not result in genetic modifications so that those in enhanced nature bodies in the eternal state are
almost human. The Lord’s return will put an end to any form of transhumanism and posthumanism that would lead
to anyone becoming Nephilim. Never again will either angels or humans attempt to transgress their bounds and
become a different kind of creature.
                                                      Multiverse
Additional Universes
       Dillow, Alcorn, and Chitwood are correct that human beings will someday rule the galaxies.22 The most
reasonable corollary, accordingly, is that human procreation will continue in eternity future. The human population
will one day fill the current galaxies of our universe. The technical differentiation just interjected with the word
current is due to the YEC cosmological model adopted herein, which was pioneered by Russ Humphreys and
adapted by John Hartnett. The universe is finite and bounded. Basically, the universe is a large sphere, finite in size.
An objection might be raised that since the universe is finite, the human population cannot expand infinitely. Alcorn
responds to this possible limitation to infinite growth with two suggestions: “It may be that Christ’s government
will always increase because he will continually create new worlds to govern (and, perhaps, new creatures to inhabit
those new worlds). Or perhaps it will always increase because the new universe though still finite, may be so vast
that what Christ creates in a moment will never be exhaustively known by finite beings.”23
       Although Alcorn’s suggestion is helpful, I personally find it too small scale. Even if quasars in our universe
are embryonic galaxies being ejected from mature galaxies, so that new galaxies are being formed, it still seems
that the finite amount of mass and energy that went into the creation of this universe would fail eventually to provide
sufficient habitation for an infinitely expanding human population. Therefore, I adopt a multiverse model, though
certainly not of the sci-fi variety where an infinite number of finite universes are assumed so that eventually you
would find a clone of yourself doing the same thing that you are doing in one of those universes. Far from it!24

knees is enough to disprove the Dillowian-Chitwoodian argument that all forms of death must be obliterated by the
apocalyptic promise.

       Alcorn suggests that God will create new worlds. In that vein, I propose that the Lord will create new
universes.25 Suppose that the current universe has a hundred billion galaxies, a very conservative estimation to be
sure. Further suppose that there will be one billion overcomers. Eventually, on an average, by the time the population
in our current universe reaches full capacity, an overcomer would be ruling one hundred galaxies by those
calculations. Naturally, in my estimation, Dillow will be one of these high-ranking overcomers. In addition to his
other ministries, his book Reign has been a tremendous help to many, including myself, and his new book Destiny
is as well.26 Though I disagree with him on some maters, I greatly appreciate his book. To project that he will rule
a hundred galaxies in the present universe is a very conservative estimate. But what will he do with these galaxies
once the population of these galaxies starts to reach optimum capacity? I hypothesize that, ultimately, he will have
to teleport these galaxies to another universe or to other universes.
Moving Galaxies to Another Universe
       For those who have never considered the possibility of teleporting galaxies, we can start small. Many
recognize that overcomers will have bodies like Jesus and be able to teleport from one location to another. Would
overcomers be able to hold something as small as a marble in their hand and teleport with that marble in their hand
to another location and thus move the marble? Surely, they could. Would they be able to hold something bigger like
a briefcase? That is reasonable as well. How about something bigger like a suitcase? Of course, they would. So

universes: “If there were another copy of me present in a parallel dimension, that copy would need the redemption
of Jesus just as much as the copy of me that is writing this book....this is impossible” because it would require that
Jesus die many times rather than once (Heb 7:27). Any interaction or perception that occult seers and practitioners
may have in or about these alternate realities are not of actual realities but potential realities, a dreamlike perception
or interaction with potential parallel realities. Daniel Duval, Higher Dimensions: Parallel Dimensions & the Spirit
Realm (Bride Publications, 2016), KL 2086-2087, 2121. I believe that God will give us access to these potential
realities in the future so that we can know what would have happened if we or He had done things differently. But
the present study is more concerned with actual parallel realities rather than potential parallel realities.

of space and one of time” (p. 78). Although atheists use multiverse theory to counter the anthropic principle,

the possibility of multiple universes” (p. 87). In fact, according to astronomer Owen Gingerich, the Christian view
of Heaven seems to require multiple universes operating “precisely according to the guidelines of the Christian
empyrean” (pp. 88-89). Dinesh D’Souza, Life After Death: The Evidence (Washington, DC: Regnery Publishing,

   When it comes to distinguishing a gift from a reward, Dillow’s Destiny beats Alcorn’s Heaven hands down.

refute Alcorn: Turning from sin and following Christ are issues pertaining to behavior and thus rewards. They have
nothing to do with entering Heaven which, contrastively, is a gift.

where does one draw the line? Jesus encourages us to stretch our minds when He promises: “Truly I say to you,
whoever says to this mountain, ‘Be taken up and cast into the sea,’ and does not doubt in his heart, but believes that
what he says is going to happen, it shall be granted him” (Mk 11:23). Why presume that this promise could not

Moving mountains, by the way, only seems impossible.”27
                                    Illustration 2. 4D Teleportation of Galaxies




        If overcomers can move whatever they need to move at the proper time, as long as they have the proper place
to put it, as seems reasonable, then extrapolation would lead one to believe that they will be able to move galaxies.
First things first, though, preliminary steps would need to be taken care of, naturally. In eternity future, Dillow will
need to teleport those galaxies under his rule that are closest to Earth to remoter sectors of the present universe, long
before this universe reaches its optimum population capacity. Because Earth is at or near the center of the universe,
as proven by the red shifts (see Humphreys and Hartnett, for example), the galaxies that will reach their population
capacities the quickest will be those near Earth, which is in a galaxy at the center of the universe. To facilitate
continued population expansion, I propose that Dillow will move these highly populated galaxies to remoter sectors
of the universe long before the outer fringes of the universe are heavily populated. Surely, he will not move them
through 3D space, though, as doing so would be a logistical nightmare. Moving galaxies through 4D space would
be much more practical.28 In other words, instead of transporting galaxies, he would teleport them. We don’t want
galaxies crashing into one another! Moreover, to maintain the balance in galactic clusters, for example, he would
want to teleport an uninhabited galaxy of the same mass into the place vacated by the galaxy he is moving. We
don’t want clusters of galaxies rotating like a tire out of balance. Plus, bringing in an unpopulated galaxy from the
outer fringes of the universe to the center of the universe would facilitate growth in the center of the universe.
        In the illustration above, I picture the present universe as Universe 1, using Humphreys’ original spatial 4D
cosmological model, and hypothesize a teleportational swap of two similar galaxies. First, (A) a populated galaxy
near our Milky Way swaps places with (B) an unpopulated remote galaxy in our universe. Later, as the fringe
galaxies start to become heavily populated, Dillow will perform a second, similar teleportational swap between
(A) a populated fringe galaxy over which he rules and (B) an unpopulated galaxy in an unpopulated second universe.
He might as well teleport this populated galaxy from universe 1 to the center of this new universe 2 so that this
populated galaxy can serve as the seedbed from which to populate this second universe. In time, he will rule over
that second universe as the human population spreads throughout it.

       In my estimation, Dillow eventually will not only rule billions of galaxies in the present universe but
innumerable universes in the multiverse. Let us suppose, though, that a lowly ranking overcomer, such as myself,
is only ruling one galaxy by the time Dillow is ruling his first universe. Will I regret only ruling one galaxy while
Dillow is off ruling his own universe? Not at all.29 Overcomers will have no regrets. This hypothesis is inductively
reasonable and deductively provable. Contrastively, how about unfaithful believers who have been thrown into the
outer darkness and who, therefore, might be pictured as janitors mopping floors in the shopping malls on some
planets in some remote corners of some distant galaxies, will they have regrets? Yes. This position is both
psychologically reasonable and misthologically biblical. Yet being a janitor in Heaven is far better than being in
Hell. Thus, this model does not make a Hell out of Heaven. Better to be a janitor in Heaven than a king in Hell, as
they would say. But why be content with being a janitor in Heaven when one can be a king in Heaven, as Jesus
would say?
       In my classic model in TOD, subcomers would never be allowed back into New Jerusalem once they are cast
out of it, when the effects of the Bema are carried out. Dillow proposes that they will be allowed to live in New
Jerusalem, however. New Jerusalem will have streets and floors, so one might suppose, on Dillowian premises, that
subcomers could have janitorial positions in that city. Nevertheless, I do not believe that picturing the outer darkness
as being inside the New Jerusalem is a reasonable inference even in that instance. Alternatively, I can imagine a
theoretical scenario in which the outer darkness could be pictured as being in New Jerusalem.

                                         Illustration 4. 4D Miniaturized Galaxy




        In a popular sci-fi movie, Men in Black (MIB), a key part of the plot revolved around spatially thinking fourth
dimensionally. That modest proposal is not farfetched, of course. Acknowledging multiple dimensions is good
science and good theology. The hard-to-believe application of this model, though, is that MIB pictures the
possibility of a full-sized galaxy being contained in a marble-sized sphere. Although I am very skeptical that such
a feat is actually possible, I am open to the possibility, at least theoretically, in that I easily can imagine that fictional
reality. At the end of the movie, our own Milky Way is pictured as being inside such a marble. Picturing that
possibility is difficult because it assumes that those residing inside the marble would be oblivious to the fact that
their own galaxy is contained, hyperdimensionally, inside another sphere. I can easily conceive of that possibility
in the case of a universe, but imagining it at the level of a galaxy is much more difficult. For example, consider the
multiverse pictured above in Illustration 3. 3D Universes in Hyperspace. These universes, although adjacent, are
separated by hyperspace; therefore, we would not be aware of those other universes when limited to our 3D
perspective. We are aware, in contrast, of the 3D reality that happens outside our galaxy within our universe. Light,
for example, from other galaxies reaches our galaxy. Consequently, picturing a galaxy that is contained within a
sphere is much easier if it is posed that such a galaxy is contained within the sphere in such a manner as our universe
is contained within its sphere. After all, our universe is a finite, bound, spherically shaped sphere. I can imagine,
then, such a universe residing inside a marble-sized sphere, as depicted by MIB. By extension, I can image a galaxy
in the same placement. But, contrary to MIB, I do not propose that those within that galaxy would be aware of any
3D reality outside of their reality.
        Rucker has a well-illustrated book on multiple dimensions.30 Unfortunately, he opposes the idea of a finite,
bounded universe because in his opinion nothing could exist outside our universe if it were bounded. Thus, he thinks
that “the notion of a universe with edges is almost inconceivable.” Likewise, a simplistic atheistic position would
pose that nothing can exist beyond existence; therefore, God cannot exist outside our universe. Rucker’s objection,
that a finite bounded universe is inconceivable—because then you would have a “door into Nothing”—seems to
manifest this type of short-sighted atheistic perspective.31 I do not find such objections to be scientifically credible,
however.

                    Illustration 6. Hyperdimensional Privileged 4D Universes in Hyperspace




       Rucker and I both pose multiple 4D universes floating like bubbles in hyperspace. I simply reject his notion
that the universes are unbounded hyperdimensional spheres.37 Rather, they are each bounded by their observable
dimensions. Furthermore, our galaxy has the privileged position of being at the center of our universe. Fourth
dimensionally, following Humphreys’ original model, our Milky Way would be at the bottom of the 4D
gravitational well.38 If I were using Hartnett’s model instead, I might have to draw our universe at the top of a
gravitational hill, which is still a privileged position. Regardless of which of these three 4D shapes one might prefer,
however, the question at hand is, “What would such a universe look like on the outside?” Rucker well answers:

      What would such a hyperspace tunnel look like? The entrance to it would look like a sphere that
      contained a whole other universe, incredibly shrunken and distorted. If you dived headfirst into this
      sphere, you would feel as if you passed right through it. But then when you looked around you would
      realize that you were in the other universe now, and looking back at the hyperspace tunnel, you would
      see a sphere that seemed to contain your whole original universe, incredibly shrunken and distorted.
             There is actually a very similar object that looks just like the mouth of an Einstein-Rosen bridge:
      a glass Christmas tree ornament. Such a spherical mirror reflects, in principle, the entire universe
      around it....Of course, if you were looking at the mouth of a hyperspace tunnel to another universe,
      you would not see the mirror image of our universe, you would see what looks like the mirror image
      of another universe. (Emphasis his.)39

        He shows a picture of a man contemplating large, softball-sized, Christmas ornaments as the picture of what
this universe would look like from the outside. Looking into this universe from the outside, it would look like a
large Christmas ornament, and you would be able to see this universe, although it would appear distorted looking
at it from the outside. Whereas Rucker’s perspective appears to be limited to a hollow crystal ball, I would picture
a solid, spherical crystal ball, when thinking of the interior of that ball in 3D rather than 4D terms. If such a
multiverse model is possible, and good theology and good science concur that it is, then each overcomer might be
given access to his or her own personal universe within the Heavenly City!40

Heaven is a Different Type of Universe
       In his fictional novel, Dominion, Alcorn pictures current believers who have died and gone on to Heaven as
having just stepped inside the perimeter of Heaven. He fictionally pictures them being given a personal planet,
evidently in our current universe, which he considers to be a part of Heaven.41 They have access to planets in our
universe, but our universe is portrayed fictionally as being more fully dimensional in the heavenly portions than our
present reality on Earth. Granted, our reality is only a shadow of that heavenly realm. Yet, contrary to Alcorn, the
higher dimension casting a shadow into our dimension should not be understood as part of our dimension. A 3D
object casts a 2D shadow. Likewise, a 4D object would cast a 3D shadow. But by presenting these personalized 4D
planets simultaneously as part of the present 3D universe and part of the 4D Heaven, Alcorn has placed himself in
an unnecessary quandary. By indicating that the unique, personalized colors exist on planets and that a fuller
dimensionality is found there than in our Shadowlands (the term he applies to Earth), he has painted a picture of
these heavenly planets that is more at home in a heavenly universe than in our own universe, where the laws of
physics would limit the color spectrum to what we currently experience. Rather than merge our universe with
Heaven, as Alcorn has done, one would be better to follow Putnam and Horn in interpreting Heaven, the third
heaven (2Cor 12:2), to be entirely distinct from our present universe:

      In pharisaical thought, the first heaven was simply the place where the birds fly, anything removed
      from and not attached to the surface of the Earth. On the other end of the spectrum and of a different
      substance was the third heaven—the dwelling place of God. This was the place from which angelic
      spheres spread outward. Between this third heaven, “where dwells the throne room of God,” and the
      first heaven, where the birds fly, was a war zone called the “second heaven”—the place where Satan
      abides as the prince of the power of the “air,” a sort of gasket heaven, the domain of Satan
      encompassing the surface of the Earth. Thus, Satan’s kingdom is the atmosphere above Earth, not
      beneath it (or in the center crust of it) in hell.42 (Italics theirs.)

      Biblically, the heavenly universe is of a different substance than our own universe, with a different law of
physics. Ross explains that when our universe is made new, it will have a different law of physics than it does now:
“‘Physical’ will have a new meaning. All the forces and laws of physics will be changed.”43 Ross immediately
appeals to the literal nature of the New Jerusalem to support his point:

    Evidence that gravity will be different or nonexistent in the new creation comes from the biblical description
    of the New Jerusalem....If the familiar force of gravity were in operation, this cube would collapse into
    spherical shape, for in our universe, any material object with dimensions exceeding about 300 miles across
    would be pulled by gravity into a more or less spherical shape.
           We cannot assume, however, that the new creation will be devoid of any kind of physicality....It is
    hard to conceive, too, of nonphysical gates, streets, walls, and mountains.44

       New physics will apply to our new universe just as they apply currently to the heavenly universe. The same
Heavenly City that now resides in Heaven will reside in orbit above the new Earth. Ross’ scientific precision in
favor of literalicity is appreciated.45 Likewise, Alcorn uses his fictional novel as his apologetic tool for literalicity,
in a three-way conversation between Dani (a believer who has just recently entered Heaven), Torel (her guardian
angel who brought her there), and C. S. Lewis (who has been there for years). Torel explains, “The great city will
one day be moved to the new earth, and at last you will enter the place he has made for you.” Like Dillow, Dani
responds, “Somehow I never envisioned this city as an actual place. I thought the descriptions were figurative.”
“Torel looked perplexed, while Lewis smiled. ‘What does a figurative place look like?’ Torel asked. ‘How do you

a galaxy would be necessary as well. But a galaxy seems to need other galaxies; therefore, the most reasonable
postulation is that overcomers would be given personal universes.

      the “chariot of the Lord flew.” This woodcut ably illustrates the ancient conception of the heavens and
      their tripartite division, a conception that remained dominant in some circles, particularly
      fundamentalist ones, until well after the Enlightenment.48 (Emphasis his.)

       This is one interpretation of the woodcut. There are others: “It has been used to represent a supposedly
medieval cosmology, including a flat earth bounded by a solid and opaque sky, or firmament, and also as a
metaphorical illustration of either the scientific or the mystical quests for knowledge.”49 For sake of argument, I
will adopt this picture as a rough sketch of my view of the third heaven. After all, I am a fundamentalist and a
creationist, and Elwell seems to have little regard for either. Even so, I find this rudimentary picture of the third
heaven much more biblically and scientifically accurate than that posed by Elwell.

      Because I believe the universe is bounded and spherical, it is natural to ask, “Would you see Heaven if you
poked your head through the outer boundaries of the universe?” The typical Flammarion picture gives the
impression that you would see Heaven if you could reach the edge of the universe and poke your head through it.
In my understanding, though, you would not—not unless you simultaneously poked your head through a teleportal.
        Illustration 8. Flammarion Poking His Head through the Edge of the Universe into Hyperspace




        The portal makes the difference. Without it, you are just extending the boundaries of your universe in a little
bubble into hyperspace. But you do not have to travel to the outer perimeter of the universe to access a portal. Take
the recent movie, Heaven Is for Real, for instance. In this movie, the young boy sees a portal to Heaven and angels
flying in Heaven on the other side of the portal. If he were to walk up to the portal (doorway to Heaven) and place
his head and hand through the portal, the rest of his body would still be in our dimension while his head and hand
were in the heavenly dimension. This would be easy to depict in a movie. From our perception, walking through
the portal would be just like walking from one room into another through a doorway.
        Yet actually, or so it would seem, as he stepped through the portal, the molecules of his body would be
transferred across the universe, through the outer edge of the universe, and into the heavenly sphere. For such
reason, sci-fi movies seem to find it preferable to picture one’s entire body transferring through an intermediary
wormhole. Perhaps some portals work like that, but certainly not all portals.
        At Jesus’ baptism, “immediately coming up out of the water, He saw the heavens opening, and the Spirit like
a dove descending upon Him” (Mk 1:10). The Holy Spirit moved seamlessly from one dimension to the other, such
as what one would have anticipated if a dove flew through the portal depicted in Heaven Is for Real, in moving
from the heavenly realm to our earthly realm on that occasion. This is the proper biblical imagery from Stephen’s
account also when “he said, ‘Behold, I see the heavens opened up and the Son of Man standing at the right hand of
God’” (Acts 7:56). Other similar biblical accounts include: Gen 28:12; Rev 4:1; Rev 11:12. The biblical impression
is that you can move from one dimension to another without having to take a trip through a wormhole.
        Such a perspective is far more biblically and scientifically appealing than Elwell’s theory that God is riding
around on Planet X, that Paul was caught up to Planet X, that Planet X is Heaven, and that believers will be taken
to Heaven/Planet X via the rainbow bridge, Bifrost.50 Elwell attempts to demythologize Heaven and turn it into a
big, black, frozen asteroid the size of a planet that keeps slamming into other planets like a cue ball on a billiard
table, all the while being bombarded with radiation.51 A fundamentalist, such as myself, posing an extradimensional
Heaven seems much more reasonable.

Personal Universe
       Hutchings’ book is dedicated to the thesis that the Great Pyramid of Giza (GPG) is a picture of the literal
New Jerusalem. Like Alcorn, he believes that “each Christian may have his own planet.”52 Such proposals
(concerning a personal planet) and my proposal (regarding a personal universe) are not mutually exclusive. In
addition to being given a personal planet in our current universe, overcomers might also be given their own personal
universe, seemingly contained in (what appears to be from the outside) a miniaturized crystal sphere. Inside the
sphere, nonetheless, it would be a full-sized universe. To make this theoretical model easier to grasp (pun intended),
imagine that the sphere is a crystal ball the size of a softball, sitting on a table in the center of an overcomer’s living
room which, in turn, is inside his or her heavenly mansion within New Jerusalem. By laying their hands on the
sphere, overcomers can teleport to the desired location within the sphere. If so, the heavenly mansions being
prepared for them in New Jerusalem would include their own universe, accessible through externally miniaturized
spheres inside their living rooms. That miniaturized portal to their universe would be part of their room, indeed part
of the furniture within their room.53
       Evidently, John saw something outside our universe when he said, “I saw a great white throne and Him who
sat upon it, from whose presence earth and heaven fled away, and no place was found for them” (Rev 20:11). This
scene takes place in a sphere of reality where light from our universe is not accessible to those within that sphere.
The sphere of reality being described by John appears to be a dimension outside our universe. Light external to this
sphere seems to be absent inside the sphere, which is what I would expect inside a hyperdimensional bubble. If this
conjecture is correct, then one also might hypothesize that the Lake of Fire is also a sphere of reality outside our
universe. The working hypothesis herein will be that the external hyperspace inside and outside of the multiverse
is black. The Lake of Fire also could be perceived as a 4D bubble floating in the “black darkness” of hyperspace
(2Pet 2:17; Jude 1:13), particularly if the energy emitted by this dark entity is outside the visible color spectrum. A
microwave is very hot but emits energy outside our visible spectrum. If the Lake of Fire likewise uses invisible
energy it would be black internally in 3D. Thus, if viewed externally from the perspective of hyperspace, the Lake
of Fire would be a black bubble floating in the black darkness. Perhaps there will even be a place in our universe or

    In my theoretical proposal, the personalized universe is not actually miniaturized but only appears to be

undergo a miniaturization at the molecular level. Moreover, those who have undergone the miniaturization are
acutely aware that they have undergone such miniaturization and are able to interact directly with those who have
not undergone the miniaturization. I am not posing a molecular miniaturization but only a miniaturization that is
phenomenally apparent, exclusively to those outside that sphere of reference. As a corollary, those inside the
miniaturized sphere would have no direct perception of, much less direct interaction with, those outside the sphere.
Those outside could see into the sphere, but those on the inside of the sphere would not be able to see out of the
sphere. My reconstruction is very much like MIB, with the obvious exception that I would not be able to place our
Milky Way inside such a miniaturized sphere; for we are very much aware of the extension of our universe beyond
such fictional boundaries. In my reconstruction, those inside such boundaries would be aware of such boundaries,
just as those residing at the furthest regions of a universe would be aware of their boundaries. They would not be
able to move in their 3D reality beyond the furthermost point of their 3D reality without going into hyperspace. As
a corollary, they would not be able to see the light from other universes. Moreover, I am posing that an entire
universe is enclosed because that is the scientific model that is most often entertained. Accordingly, the
miniaturized sphere, as entertained herein, is merely a bridge to another full-sized 3D universe floating in
hyperspace, as pictured in Illustration 5. When the spheres are viewed from such an external 4D spatial point of
reference in hyperspace, they would appear to be the size of a softball. Likewise, when the entrance to one of these
universes is viewed through an Einstein-Rosen bridge from the inside of another universe, the entrance would be
perceived as a small spherical ball by those who are viewing the portal, as illustrated by Rucker (Dimension, 118,
fig. 118). In other words, this vantage point would produce the MIB phenomena as applied to a seemingly
miniaturized universe, though in actuality the universe being viewed inside the sphere is not miniaturized regarding
its own 3D point of reference.

Access to the Outer Darkness
       If that is the case, then the principle of correlativity would suggest that the biblical outer darkness is also
accessible via a miniaturized sphere. And if that is the case, then one could pose that the outer darkness is accessed
through a miniaturized sphere inside of New Jerusalem. By building one extrapolation upon another, a possible
scenario can be entertained in which the outer darkness technically could be, in some sense of the word, inside New
Jerusalem. Dillow insists upon placing the outer darkness inside the city if the city is taken literally. My
accommodation of that model would propose that, if this is the case, then the outer darkness is inside the city in the
sense that a miniaturized sphere within New Jerusalem will allow residences in New Jerusalem to see and access
the former abode of New Jerusalem, that is, the platform (or planet) where the city once stood in the third heaven.54
This proposal synthesizes Crawford’s model and my model with the perimeter perspective suggested by Alcorn.
       From Alcorn’s perimeter perspective, believers can stand, evidently on one of the planets or on a platform in
the heavenly universe, outside of New Jerusalem and watch it being built. But they cannot enter the city yet. This
outer-courtyard perspective is in complete harmony with Crawford’s perspective. Alcorn fictionally leads the reader
to consider an outer courtyard, so to speak, in a fuller dimensional heavenly universe, as providing the staging
ground from which the heavenly citizens currently can watch the city being built.55
Out of Heaven
        In the Crawfordian model, as Crawford and I initially developed it, I wrongly posed something much more
modest. I pictured the composite—the large block and the city—as Heaven itself.56 I failed to distinguish the city
and its courtyard from Heaven itself. In other words, the city and its courtyard are only a part of this alternate
heavenly dimension. Current heavenly citizens reside in this alternate dimension called Heaven. The city could not
come out of Heaven if the city comprised Heaven, but the city does come out of Heaven (Rev 21:2,10)! So let us
not equate the city with Heaven. Also, if the city’s courtyard is an entire planet or the size of a planet—in another
universe no less!—which is one possibility, then the Lord would not bring that entire planet with Him. Certainly,
only the Heavenly City itself would be teleported to Earth, which is the model I posed in my Caulian model.57 But
at that time, like Dillow, I mistakenly had a vague notion that the city comprised Heaven. When Crawford posed a
courtyard outside of the city, I initially did not expand my view of Heaven sufficiently. The time has come to
correct that deficiency.

is the AM station and Hades is the FM station. You would have to turn the dimensional dial of your mole machine
to the local FM station when you reached the desired location, thus tuning into that reality in order make a
hyperdimensional jump from Earth into that alternate dimension—a smaller, bounded, alternate sphere of reality.58

One might wonder if Earth is an alternate dimensional subcompartment of Heaven, as Hades is of Earth. Is Heaven
all around us as a parallel universe in the same way Earth is all around those in Hades in a parallel dimension? No.
The perception of Earth being in Heaven as an overlapping subset is an oversimplification. The Bible describes
Satan and his forces being cast out of Heaven down to Earth as a result of losing their war with Michael and his
angels (Rev 12:7-13). Heaven and Earth do not overlap. Nevertheless, Earth is down in relation to Heaven, just as
Hades is down in relation to Earth. Regardless of whether you are at the North Pole or South Pole, if you were to
leave the surface of Earth and go to Hades, you would go down. You would be leaving the surface and traveling
down to an alternate dimensional subsphere, just as anyone on the surface of the ocean and diving to the bottom of
the ocean would be considered as going down. Likewise, Earth is better perceived to be a subsphere inside of the
larger sphere of Heaven, but in a non-overlapping sense, just as the land mass at the bottom of the ocean does not
overlap with the ocean waters above. They are two different spheres of reality.
                                            Illustration 11. Three Heavens




       As noted above, a biblical cosmology must be guided by Paul’s description of being caught up to the third
heaven (2Cor 12:2). The proper deduction is that the Heavenly City resides in the third heaven. The city does not
comprise the third heaven any more than a city on Earth would comprise Earth. Just as New York is on Earth but
does not comprise Earth, much less our universe, so the Heavenly City is in Heaven but does not comprise Heaven.
Our Earth is in the center of our universe. Earth is enlarged in the illustration to make it visible. The first heaven is
Earth’s atmosphere. The second heaven is the 3D universe in which Earth resides. The third heaven is the heavenly
universe in which our 3D universe resides. Similar to the way the first heaven is made up of a different composition
than the second heaven, so the third heaven would be made up of a different substance than the second heaven.
Perhaps that is all there is to the present cosmology, which is certainly very good cosmology in its own rights. Amos
describes God as “The One who builds His upper chambers in the heavens, and has founded His vaulted dome over
the earth” (Amos 9:6). In my cosmological model, Heaven would be a vaulted dome over Earth regardless of where
one is standing on Earth. No matter if you are standing, either at the North Pole or South Pole, the third heaven is a
dome above you, surrounding the universe in which you live.
       Heaven is the outer sphere of where we live; our universe is the intermediate sphere in which we live; the
Earth is the inner sphere on which we live.59 These spheres do not overlap; rather, the first sphere is contained
within the second and the second within the third. Even if this is the current state of affairs, it will not be the eternal
state of affairs as more universes are created like ours, and those universes likewise reside within the hyperspace
inside the heavenly sphere. Eventually, if not already, a multiverse must exist within the heavenly sphere.
Nonetheless, this model still complies with the information provided by Amos. My multiverse hypothesis still poses
Heaven as the dome above us. The Bible teaches that God already “has prepared a city” for those believers, like
Abraham, who earnestly desire a better one, a heavenly one (Heb 11:16). The Reward City already exists. Similarly,
we are told, “Eye has not seen, nor ear has heard, nor the heart of man has imagined, all that God has prepared for
those who love Him” (1Cor 2:9; TM). Rewards that are going to blow our imagination are already in place, already

       As to the location of the outer darkness, I reject Dillow’s notion that the outer darkness is in New Jerusalem,
though I would allow the proposal that the outer darkness is accessible from within the Heavenly City via a
hyperdimensional doorway. We know from eyewitness accounts that hyperdimensional doorways to various places
exist.63
       The genius of Crawford’s model is to propose that the outer darkness is the outer courtyard of the Heavenly
City, wherever that courtyard may be located currently. Initially, when Crawford and I were working on his model,
I proposed a box-shaped courtyard. Even if that were to be the case, the question that must be asked is, “Why bring
the outer court with Him? Those in the courtyard would be moved from the courtyard to the Bema arena atop the
city (or within the city) when the city is moved from Heaven to Earth so that those being raptured can be brought
up to join them at the Bema. There is no reason for the Lord to bring the courtyard with Him unless it is for the
specific purpose of casting those who fail to pass the Bema back out to the courtyard just outside the city, as was
posed in the original Crawfordian model. However, one could just as easily pose that they are cast, by means of a
hyperdimensional doorway, back to the courtyard that remained in the heavenly realm.
       In the multiverse model above, the courtyard is readily seen to be in the heavenly realm that comprises the
outer shell of the multiverse. Suggesting that the outer darkness is in the outer shell certainly seems intuitive.
Therefore, in this revised Crawfordian model, which I will term the MACC (Multiverse Alcorn-Crawfordian-
Caulian) model, I am entertaining the possibility that the outer courtyard is the place where the redeemed currently
are watching the construction of New Jerusalem. That courtyard will remain where it is in the heavenly realm when
the Lord comes with the Heavenly City to Earth at the time of the rapture. That courtyard may be a planet or a large
box-shaped structure or something else.64 Regardless, the courtyard stays put when the Lord returns. When one is
launching a rocket, one does not launch the launching pad with the rocket. The courtyard is little more than the
heavenly launch pad and the construction site for the Heavenly City, the mothership, which is to launch to Earth at
the time of the rapture. Consequently, those believers who are found unfaithful at the Bema will be cast back to the
heavenly realm—to the launching pad or planet from which the Heavenly City is launched. For those cast back to
the courtyard, that courtyard, which they are currently enjoying in anticipation of the Heavenly City, will, at that
time, become their outer darkness. Presumably, they will be confined to that corner of the heavenly universe for all
eternity, as is indicated by being bound hand and foot when cast therein (Mt 22:13). The heavenly shell is not hell.
So the objection that this model makes a hell out of heaven is fallacious.




So one might speculate that unfallen ETs from other universes might do the same. However, the Bible does not lead
us to expect any such alien saviors, only alien masqueraders. Therefore, realistically, the only ETs mankind is likely
to experience this side of the second coming are false aliens: malevolent EDs impersonating benevolent ETs.
     On the other hand, surely other 3D universes like our own have plants and animals. The universes we are to
rule would not be devoid of animal and plant life! Further, I would not be surprised if talking animals in other
universes await our discovery. Alcorn thinks that some of the animals of our own planet may have been able to talk
before the fall (Heaven, 389-390). If this is the case, and it seems reasonable, then some animals in unfallen
universes may be able to speak as well, even now. If these other universes are in an unfallen state, though, one must
pose a hypothesis as to why a fall did not occur in those universes. Why are they not subject to the hybridization
that is occurring on this planet? Why are fallen angels not experimenting with the plant and animal DNA in those
universes? One possibility is that these other universes may not have Adam-Eve equivalents that Satan could tempt
and who, therefore, could open the doors of their universe to him. This hypothesis presupposes the creationist model
in which the Luciferian fall occurred after the creation of Adam and Eve and is limited, in terms of its repercussions
with reproducing creatures, to our cosmos/universe. Other universes have no Adam-Eve rulers capable of unlocking
the doors of their universe to Satan. The doors of their 3D reality are locked by God and can only be unlocked by
mankind. This hypothesis practically nullifies the theoretical conjecture regarding unfallen ETs existing in unfallen
universes. Talking animals do not constitute ETs. Occam’s Razor renders this planet-animal-closed-door hypothesis
more plausible than the theoretical possibility of unfallen ETs.

   Stargates are one such example. Thomas Horn, Zenith 2016: Did Something Begin in the Year 2012 that will
